## Introduction

Having proved a preservation property in the last chapter, a natural
next step would be to prove progress. That is, to prove a property
of the form

    If Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v, then either M is a lambda abstraction or M â€”â†’ N for some N.

Such a property would tell us that having a denotation implies either
reduction to normal form or divergence. This is indeed true, but we
can prove a much stronger property! In fact, having a denotation that
is a function value (not `âŠ¥`) implies reduction to a lambda
abstraction.

This stronger property, reformulated a bit, is known as _adequacy_.
That is, if a term `M` is denotationally equal to a lambda abstraction,
then `M` reduces to a lambda abstraction.

    â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)  implies M â€”â†  Æ› N' for some N'

Recall that `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)` is equivalent to saying that `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦
w)` for some `v` and `w`. We will show that `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` implies
multi-step reduction a lambda abstraction.  The recursive structure of
the derivations for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` are completely different from
the structure of multi-step reductions, so a direct proof would be
challenging. However, The structure of `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` closer to
that of [BigStep]({{ site.baseurl }}/BigStep/) call-by-name
evaluation. Further, we already proved that big-step evaluation
implies multi-step reduction to a lambda (`cbnâ†’reduce`). So we shall
prove that `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` implies that `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c`, where `c` is a
closure (a term paired with an environment), `Î³'` is an environment
that maps variables to closures, and `Î³` and `Î³'` are appropriate
related.  The proof will be an induction on the derivation of
`Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, and to strengthen the induction hypothesis, we will relate
semantic values to closures using a _logical relation_ `ğ•`.

The rest of this chapter is organized as follows.

* To make the `ğ•` relation down-closed with respect to `âŠ‘`,
  we must loosen the requirement that `M` result in a function value and
  instead require that `M` result in a value that is greater than or
  equal to a function value. We establish several properties about
  being ``greater than a function''.

* We define the logical relation `ğ•` that relates values and closures,
  and extend it to a relation on terms `ğ”¼` and environments `ğ”¾`.
  We prove several lemmas that culminate in the property that
  if `ğ• v c` and `vâ€² âŠ‘ v`, then `ğ• vâ€² c`.

* We prove the main lemma,
  that if `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'` and `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, then `ğ”¼ v (clos M Î³')`.

* We prove adequacy as a corollary to the main lemma.

## The property of being greater or equal to a function

We define the following short-hand for saying that a value is
greather-than or equal to a function value.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="above-fun"></a><a id="4190" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4190" class="Function">above-fun</a> <a id="4200" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="4202" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4151" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="4208" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="4210" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>

If a value `u` is greater than a function, then an even greater value `u'`
is too.

The bottom value `âŠ¥` is not greater than a function.

If the join of two values `u` and `u'` is greater than a function, then
at least one of them is too.

On the other hand, if neither of `u` and `u'` is greater than a function,
then their join is also not greater than a function.

</pre>{% endraw %}
The converse is also true. If the join of two values is not above a
function, then neither of them is individually.

</pre>{% endraw %}
The property of being greater than a function value is decidable, as
exhibited by the following function.

## Relating values to closures

Next we relate semantic values to closures.  The relation `ğ•` is for
closures whose term is a lambda abstraction, i.e., in weak-head normal
form (WHNF). The relation ğ”¼ is for any closure. Roughly speaking,
`ğ”¼ v c` will hold if, when `v` is greater than a function value, `c` evaluates
to a closure `c'` in WHNF and `ğ• v c'`. Regarding `ğ• v c`, it will hold when
`c` is in WHNF, and if `v` is a function, the body of `c` evaluates
according to `v`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="ğ•"></a><a id="7244" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7244" class="Function">ğ•</a> <a id="7246" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7248" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4151" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="7254" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7256" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#2467" class="Datatype">Clos</a> <a id="7261" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7263" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="ğ”¼"></a><a id="7267" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7267" class="Function">ğ”¼</a> <a id="7269" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7271" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4151" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="7277" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7279" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#2467" class="Datatype">Clos</a> <a id="7284" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7286" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
We define `ğ•` as a function from values and closures to `Set` and not as a
data type because it is mutually recursive with `ğ”¼` in a negative
position (to the left of an implication).  We first perform case
analysis on the term in the closure. If the term is a variable or
application, then `ğ•` is false (`Bot`). If the term is a lambda
abstraction, we define `ğ•` by recursion on the value, which we
describe below.

* If the value is `âŠ¥`, then the result is true (`âŠ¤`).

* If the value is a join (u âŠ” v), then the result is the pair
  (conjunction) of ğ• is true for both u and v.

* The important case is for a function value `v â†¦ w` and closure
  `clos (Æ› N) Î³`. Given any closure `c` such that `ğ”¼ v c`, if `w` is
  greater than a function, then `N` evaluates (with `Î³` extended with `c`)
  to some closure `c'` and we have `ğ• w c'`.


The definition of `ğ”¼` is straightforward. If `v` is a greater than a
function, then `M` evaluates to a closure related to `v`.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="8538" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7267" class="Function">ğ”¼</a> <a id="8540" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8550" class="Bound">Î³&#39;</a><a id="8552" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8554" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8556" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4190" class="Function">above-fun</a> <a id="8566" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8540" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="8568" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8570" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#911" class="Function">Î£[</a> <a id="8573" href="{% endraw %}{{ id="8577" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#2467" class="Datatype">Clos</a> <a id="8582" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#911" class="Function">]</a> <a id="8584" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8550" class="Bound">Î³&#39;</a> <a id="8587" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#3021" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="8589" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8548" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="8591" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#3021" class="Datatype Operator">â‡“</a> <a id="8593" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8573" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="8595" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Product.html#1162" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a> <a id="8597" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7244" class="Function">ğ•</a> <a id="8599" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8540" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="8601" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8573" class="Bound">c</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The proof of the main lemma is by induction on `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, so it goes
underneath lambda abstractions and must therefore reason about open
terms (terms with variables). So we must relate environments of
semantic values to environments of closures.  In the following, `ğ”¾`
relates `Î³` to `Î³'` if the corresponding values and closures are related
by `ğ”¼`.

We need a few properties of the `ğ•` and `ğ”¼` relations.  The first is that
a closure in the `ğ•` relation must be in weak-head normal form.  We
define WHNF has follows.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="9400" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="WHNF"></a><a id="9405" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9405" class="Datatype">WHNF</a> <a id="9410" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9412" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="9414" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9415" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9415" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9417" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9417" class="Bound">A</a><a id="9418" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9420" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9422" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9415" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9424" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="9426" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9417" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9428" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9430" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9434" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="WHNF.Æ›_"></a><a id="9442" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9442" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›_</a> <a id="9445" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9447" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="9449" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9450" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9450" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="9451" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9453" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9454" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9454" class="Bound">N</a> <a id="9456" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9458" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9450" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9460" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3191" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="9462" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a> <a id="9464" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="9466" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="9467" class="Symbol">}</a>
     <a id="9474" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9476" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9405" class="Datatype">WHNF</a> <a id="9481" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9482" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4382" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="9484" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9454" class="Bound">N</a><a id="9485" class="Symbol">)</a>

The proof goes by cases on the term in the closure.

       <a id="9599" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9601" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7244" class="Function">ğ•</a> <a id="9603" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9589" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="9605" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9606" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#2486" class="InductiveConstructor">clos</a> <a id="9611" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9578" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="9613" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9563" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="9614" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="9616" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9618" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9405" class="Datatype">WHNF</a> <a id="9623" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9578" class="Bound">M</a>

</pre>{% endraw %}
Next we have an introduction rule for `ğ•` that mimics the `âŠ”-intro`
rule. If both `u` and `v` are related to a closure `c`, then their join is
too.

</pre>{% endraw %}
In a moment we prove that `ğ•` is preserved when going from a greater
value to a lesser value: if `ğ• v c` and `v' âŠ‘ v`, then `ğ• v' c`.
This property, named `ğ•-sub`, is needed by the main lemma in
the case for the `sub` rule.

To prove `ğ•-sub`, we in turn need the following property concerning
values that are not greater than a function, that is, values that are
equivalent to `âŠ¥`. In such cases, `ğ• v (clos (Æ› N) Î³')` is trivially true.

The proofs of `ğ•-sub` and `ğ”¼-sub` are intertwined.

link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7267" class="Function">ğ”¼</a> <a id="11046" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11021" class="Bound">v&#39;</a> <a id="11049" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11009" class="Bound">c</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
We prove `ğ•-sub` by case analysis on the closure's term, to dispatch the
cases for variables and application. We then proceed by induction on
`v' âŠ‘ v`. We describe each case below.

<a id="12844" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="12848" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="12850" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Sum.Base.html#662" class="InductiveConstructor">injâ‚</a> <a id="12855" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12855" class="Bound">af2</a> <a id="12859" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12861" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Empty.html#294" class="Function">âŠ¥-elim</a> <a id="12868" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12869" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Relation.Nullary.Negation.html#809" class="Function">contradiction</a> <a id="12883" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12855" class="Bound">af2</a> <a id="12887" class="Bound">naf2</a><a id="12891" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="12893" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="12897" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="12899" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Sum.Base.html#687" class="InductiveConstructor">injâ‚‚</a> <a id="12904" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12904" class="Bound">af3</a> <a id="12908" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12910" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Data.Empty.html#294" class="Function">âŠ¥-elim</a> <a id="12917" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12918" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v1.1/Relation.Nullary.Negation.html#809" class="Function">contradiction</a> <a id="12932" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12904" class="Bound">af3</a> <a id="12936" class="Bound">naf3</a><a id="12940" class="Symbol">)</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
* Case `âŠ‘-bot`. We immediately have `ğ• âŠ¥ (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `âŠ‘-conj-L`.

        vâ‚' âŠ‘ v     vâ‚‚' âŠ‘ v
        -------------------
        (vâ‚' âŠ” vâ‚‚') âŠ‘ v

  The induction hypotheses gives us `ğ• vâ‚' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`
  and `ğ• vâ‚‚' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`, which is all we need for this case.

* Case `âŠ‘-conj-R1`.

        v' âŠ‘ vâ‚
        -------------
        v' âŠ‘ (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)

  The induction hypothesis gives us `ğ• v' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `âŠ‘-conj-R2`.

        v' âŠ‘ vâ‚‚
        -------------
        v' âŠ‘ (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)

  Again, the induction hypothesis gives us `ğ• v' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `âŠ‘-trans`.

        v' âŠ‘ vâ‚‚   vâ‚‚ âŠ‘ v
        -----------------
             v' âŠ‘ v

  The induction hypothesis for `vâ‚‚ âŠ‘ v` gives us
  `ğ• vâ‚‚ (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`. We apply the induction hypothesis
  for `v' âŠ‘ vâ‚‚` to conclude that `ğ• v' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `âŠ‘-dist`. This case  is the most difficult. We have

        ğ• (v â†¦ w) (clos (Æ› N) Î³)
        ğ• (v â†¦ w') (clos (Æ› N) Î³)

  and need to show that

        ğ• (v â†¦ (w âŠ” w')) (clos (Æ› N) Î³)

  Let `c` be an arbtrary closure such that `ğ”¼ v c`.
  Assume `w âŠ” w'` is greater than a function.
  Unfortunately, this does not mean that both `w` and `w'`
  are above functions. But thanks to the lemma `above-fun-âŠ”`,
  we know that at least one of them is greater than a function.

  * Suppose both of them are greater than a function.  Then we have
    `Î³ âŠ¢ N â‡“ clos L Î´` and `ğ• w (clos L Î´)`.  We also have `Î³ âŠ¢ N â‡“ câ‚ƒ` and
    `ğ• w' câ‚ƒ`.  Because the big-step semantics is deterministic, we have
    `câ‚ƒ â‰¡ clos L Î´`. Also, from `ğ• w (clos L Î´)` we know that `L â‰¡ Æ› N'`
    for some `N'`. We conclude that `ğ• (w âŠ” w') (clos (Æ› N') Î´)`.

  * Suppose one of them is greater than a function and the other is
    not: say `above-fun w` and `Â¬ above-fun w'`. Then from
    `ğ• (v â†¦ w) (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`
    we have `Î³ âŠ¢ N â‡“ clos L Î³â‚` and `ğ• w (clos L Î³â‚)`. From this we have
    `L â‰¡ Æ› N'` for some `N'`. Meanwhile, from `Â¬ above-fun w'` we have
    `ğ• w' (clos L Î³â‚)`. We conclude that
    `ğ• (w âŠ” w') (clos (Æ› N') Î³â‚)`.


The proof of `sub-ğ”¼` is direct and explained below.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="15054" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#10999" class="Function">sub-ğ”¼</a> <a id="15060" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15061" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/BigStep.md %}{% raw %}#2486" class="InductiveConstructor">clos</a> <a id="15066" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15066" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="15068" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15068" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="15069" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="15071" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15072" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15072" class="Bound">v</a><a id="15073" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="15075" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15076" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15076" class="Bound">v&#39;</a><a id="15078" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="15080" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15080" class="Bound">ğ”¼v</a> <a id="15083" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15083" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a> <a id="15088" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15088" class="Bound">fv&#39;</a>
    <a id="15096" class="Keyword">with</a> <a id="15101" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15080" class="Bound">ğ”¼v</a> <a id="15104" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="15105" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4361" class="Function">above-fun-âŠ‘</a> <a id="15117" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15088" class="Bound">fv&#39;</a> <a id="15121" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15083" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a><a id="15125" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="15127" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="15131" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="15133" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15135" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15135" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="15137" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15139" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15141" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15141" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="15145" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15147" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15147" class="Bound">ğ•v</a> <a id="15150" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="15152" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="15154" class="Symbol">=</a>
      <a id="15162" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15164" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15135" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="15166" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15168" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15170" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15141" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="15174" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15176" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#10947" class="Function">sub-ğ•</a> <a id="15182" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15147" class="Bound">ğ•v</a> <a id="15185" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a> <a id="15190" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="15192" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
From `above-fun v'` and `v' âŠ‘ v` we have `above-fun v`.  Then with `ğ”¼ v c` we
obtain a closure `c` such that `Î³ âŠ¢ M â‡“ c` and `ğ• v c`. We conclude with an
application of `sub-ğ•` with `v' âŠ‘ v` to show `ğ• v' c`.


## Programs with function denotation terminate via call-by-name

The main lemma proves that if a term has a denotation that is above a
function, then it terminates via call-by-name. More formally, if
`Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` and `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'`, then `ğ”¼ v (clos M Î³')`. The proof is by
induction on the derivation of `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` we discuss each case below.

The following lemma, kth-x, is used in the case for the `var` rule.

* Case `var`. Looking up `x` in `Î³'` yields some closure, `clos M' Î´`,
  and from `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'` we have `ğ”¼ (Î³ x) (clos M' Î´)`. With the premise
  `above-fun (Î³ x)`, we obtain a closure `c` such that `Î´ âŠ¢ M' â‡“ c`
  and `ğ• (Î³ x) c`. To conclude `Î³' âŠ¢ x â‡“ c` via `â‡“-var`, we
  need `Î³' x â‰¡ clos M' Î´`, which is obvious, but it requires some
  Agda shananigans via the `kth-x` lemma to get our hands on it.

* Case `â†¦-elim`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ L Â· M â†“ v`.
  The induction hypothesis for `Î³ âŠ¢ L â†“ vâ‚ â†¦ v`
  gives us `Î³' âŠ¢ L â‡“ clos L' Î´` and `ğ• v (clos L' Î´)`.
  Of course, `L' â‰¡ Æ› N` for some `N`.
  By the induction hypothesis for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚`,
  we have `ğ”¼ vâ‚ (clos M Î³')`.
  Together with the premise `above-fun v` and `ğ• v (clos L' Î´)`,
  we obtain a closure `c'` such that `Î´ âŠ¢ N â‡“ c'` and `ğ• v c'`.
  We conclude that `Î³' âŠ¢ L Â· M â‡“ c'` by rule `â‡“-app`.

* Case `â†¦-intro`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ Æ› N â†“ v â†¦ w`.
  We immediately have `Î³' âŠ¢ Æ› M â‡“ clos (Æ› M) Î³'` by rule `â‡“-lam`.
  But we also need to prove `ğ• (v â†¦ w) (clos (Æ› N) Î³')`.
  Let `c` by an arbitrary closure such that `ğ”¼ v c`.
  Suppose `v'` is greater than a function value.
  We need to show that `Î³' , c âŠ¢ N â‡“ c'` and `ğ• v' c'` for some `c'`.
  We prove this by the induction hypothesis for `Î³ , v âŠ¢ N â†“ v'`
  but we must first show that `ğ”¾ (Î³ , v) (Î³' , c)`. We prove
  that by the lemma `ğ”¾-ext`, using facts `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'` and `ğ”¼ v c`.

* Case `âŠ¥-intro`. We have the premise `above-fun âŠ¥`, but that's impossible.

* Case `âŠ”-intro`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)` and `above-fun (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)`
  and need to show `Î³' âŠ¢ M â†“ c` and `ğ• (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚) c` for some `c`.
  Again, by `above-fun-âŠ”`, at least one of `vâ‚` or `vâ‚‚` is greater than
  a function.

  * Suppose both `vâ‚` and `vâ‚‚` are greater than a function value.
    By the induction hypotheses for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚` and `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚‚`
    we have `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ câ‚`, `ğ• vâ‚ câ‚`, `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ câ‚‚`, and `ğ• vâ‚‚ câ‚‚`
    for some `câ‚` and `câ‚‚`. Because `â‡“` is deterministic, we have `câ‚‚ â‰¡ câ‚`.
    Then by `ğ•âŠ”-intro` we conclude that `ğ• (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚) câ‚`.

  * Without loss of generality, suppose `vâ‚` is greater than a function
    value but `vâ‚‚` is not.  By the induction hypotheses for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚`,
    and using `ğ•â†’WHNF`, we have `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚`
    and `ğ• vâ‚ (clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚)`.
    Then because `vâ‚‚` is not greater than a function, we also have
    `ğ• vâ‚‚ (clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚)`. We conclude that `ğ• (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚) (clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚)`.

* Case `sub`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, `v' âŠ‘ v`, and `above-fun v'`.
  We need to show that `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c` and `ğ• v' c` for some `c`.
  We have `above-fun v` by `above-fun-âŠ‘`,
  so the induction hypothesis for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` gives us a closure `c`
  such that `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c` and `ğ• v c`. We conclude that `ğ• v' c` by `sub-ğ•`.


## Proof of denotational adequacy

From the main lemma we can directly show that `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)` implies
that `M` big-steps to a lambda, i.e., `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› Nâ€²) Î³`.

    <a id="21436" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="21438" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="21440" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="21442" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="21444" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#21426" class="Bound">Nâ€²</a> <a id="21447" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="21449" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="21451" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="21453" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="21455" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="21459" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a>  <a id="21462" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="21464" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#209" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a>
</pre>{% endraw %}
The proof goes as follows. We derive `âˆ… âŠ¢ Æ› N â†“ âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥` and
then `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)` gives us `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â†“ âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥`. We conclude
by applying the main lemma to obtain `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› Nâ€²) Î³`
for some `Nâ€²` and `Î³`.

Now to prove the adequacy property. We apply the above
lemma to obtain `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› Nâ€²) Î³` and then
apply `cbnâ†’reduce` to conclude.

## Call-by-name is equivalent to beta reduction

As promised, we return to the question of whether call-by-name
evaluation is equivalent to beta reduction. In chapter
[BigStep]({{ site.baseurl }}/BigStep/) we established the forward
direction: that if call-by-name produces a result, then the program
beta reduces to a lambda abstraction (`cbnâ†’reduce`).  We now prove the backward
direction of the if-and-only-if, leveraging our results about the
denotational semantics.

{% raw %}<pre class="Agda"><a id="reduceâ†’cbn"></a><a id="22487" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22487" class="Function">reduceâ†’cbn</a> <a id="22498" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22500" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="22502" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22503" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22503" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="22505" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22507" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="22509" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="22511" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="22512" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="22514" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22515" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22515" class="Bound">N</a> <a id="22517" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22519" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3175" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="22521" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3191" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="22523" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a> <a id="22525" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4294" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="22527" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part2/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2888" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="22528" class="Symbol">}</a>

<a id="22657" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22487" class="Function">reduceâ†’cbn</a> <a id="22668" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22668" class="Bound">Mâ€”â† Æ›N</a> <a id="22674" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="22676" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#21083" class="Function">â†“â†’â‡“</a> <a id="22680" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="22681" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Soundness.md %}{% raw %}#23358" class="Function">soundness</a> <a id="22691" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/part3/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22668" class="Bound">Mâ€”â† Æ›N</a><a id="22696" class="Symbol">)</a>

Suppose `M â€”â†  Æ› N`. Soundness of the denotational semantics gives us
`â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)`. Then by `â†“â†’â‡“` we conclude that
`âˆ…' âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› Nâ€²) Î´` for some `Nâ€²` and `Î´`.

Putting the two directions of the if-and-only-if together, we
establish that call-by-name evaluation is equivalent to beta reduction
in the following sense.
